--- Commit Message ---
LU-18635 ptlrpc: add max_mb_per_rpc_read/write parameters

Added "max_mb_per_rpc_read" and "max_mb_per_rpc_write" parameters to
get and set RPC size in terms of megabytes instead of number of pages
with "max_pages_per_rpc" parameter.

New parameters will allow the user to pass decimal values
(e.g.: 0.00390625G, 3.5M, etc.).

Parameter "max_pages_per_rpc" can now accept size values smaller
than 1M (e.g.: 768K, 0.5M, etc.).

Fix longstanding bug in sanity test_49 trying to get OST size
using 'lfs df' from OSS instead onlf client.  Instead, use new
'lfs df' options to get size directly.

Fixes: 9fe4b52ad2 ("LU-1030 osc: new IO engine implementation")

Patch Set 1:

Hello Andreas,

I don't know whom to assign PRs for review. I am assigning it to you, can you please add the right person to this PR.

In ticket, you asked to add "max_mb_per_rpc" parameter. If I am specifing it in MB, I will need to do this in float data type which is not available. If I go with fixed-point format, in that also I am not sure how many precision points will be sufficient. So I have implemented it in Bytes.

Patch Set 1: Code-Review-1

(3 comments)

This should use max_mb_per_RPC as originally requested. Using bytes is too awkward since the minimum RPC size is 64KiB and normally in the multi-MB range. 

Please also add a test case to set max_pages_per_rpc parameter and then read back max_mb_per_rpc, and also set a fractional value (eg. 3.5M) and read it back to verify it is set correctly.

--- Message (Rahul Bansal, 2025-03-13 17:35:12.000000000) ---
Patch Set 9:

> Patch Set 9:
> 
> > Patch Set 9:
> > 
> > Unfortunately, I was traveling and wasn't able to restart the testing on this patch, so it will need to be resubmitted.
> > 
> > Please use the macros that James suggested to convert the units.
> 
> Okay.

Source Code:
```
#define PAGES_TO_MiB(pages)	((pages) >> (20 - PAGE_SHIFT))
#define MiB_TO_PAGES(mb)	((mb) << (20 - PAGE_SHIFT))
```

Case max_mb_per_rpc_show() function:
    E.g: PAGE_SIZE is 4096 and number of pages 384
    PAGES_TO_Mib(): 1M ((384) >> (20 - 12))
    Wrong M size given by PAGES_TO_Mib(), values in lesser 20 bits were discarded

Case max_mb_per_rpc_store() function:
    E.g. recieved value: 1.5MiB (1572864 Bytes)
    Convert it to MiB: 1M (1572864 >> 20), lesser 20 bits were discarded
    MiB_TO_PAGES() will give wrong number of pages

PAGES_TO_MiB() and MiB_TO_PAGES() were added to round up the values to the nearest MiB (https://review.whamcloud.com/c/fs/lustre-release/+/34317). Here our purpose is to give the user flexibility of setting and getting values in decimal.

Patch Set 10: Code-Review-1

VERY sorry for the late -1 on this, but when I was discussing this at LUG last week, someone mentioned that they wanted to configure separate read and write RPC sizes.  Rather than introducing yet another overlapping parameter on the client after this one, it would be better to split this into two new parameters:

 osc.*.max_mb_per_rpc_read=N
 osc.*.max_mb_per_rpc_write=N

This will need some relatively straight forward changes to the plumbing, but I will add the description to LU-18635 so that it is more widely visible.

--- Message (Andreas Dilger, 2025-06-02 19:31:49.000000000) ---
Patch Set 11:

(6 comments)

The failures of sanity.sh test_401ga and test_401gb look like they are related to interactions between persistently setting the max_dirty_mb, and possibly left-over persistent parameters from the new test_49b that are setting max_mb_per_rpc_write, but this is later affecting max_dirty_mb when the client is being remounted in those later tests?

The other thing that I think is missing in this patch is to determine whether a read or write RPC is being generated, and then use the appropriate parameter for that.  It is clear for the readahead RPCs that the read parameter should be used, but I don't see any kind of logic like "if (read) then rpc_size = ... _read; else rpc_size = ... _write;"

Here's summary of my changes:
The changes in this patch address a compile error in a previous patch by fixing a declaration and usage issue in the `cli_brw_size` function within `lustre/include/obd.h`. Here's a summary of the changes:

- **Moved variable declaration**: The variable `mppr` (of type `u32`) was declared at the top of the function body, just after the `LASSERT` and `cli` assignment, which is now consistent with C language rules (variables must be declared before use).
- **Fixed initialization syntax**: The original code incorrectly placed the `u32 mppr = ...` declaration inline with the assignment, which caused a syntax error because the `u32` type was not properly scoped. The patch restructures this by declaring `mppr` first, then assigning it using the ternary operator.
- **Preserved logic**: The core logic remains unchanged — it computes the maximum of `cl_max_pages_per_rpc_read` and `cl_max_pages_per_rpc_write`, then shifts it left by `PAGE_SHIFT` bits to return the size in bytes.

**Summary**: This patch fixes a compile error caused by improper variable declaration placement by moving the `u32 mppr` declaration to the beginning of the function scope and restructuring the assignment to comply with C syntax rules, while preserving the original functionality.

Here's summary of my changes:
## Fix Explanation

**The Problem:**
The patch refactored the `osc_shrink_grant_to_target()` function in `lustre/osc/osc_request.c`, renaming the parameter from `target_bytes` to `tgt_bytes` for consistency. However, one reference to the old variable name `target_bytes` was missed on line 856, causing a compilation error.

**The Fix:**
Changed line 856 from:
```c
if (target_bytes >= cli->cl_avail_grant) {
```
to:
```c
if (tgt_bytes >= cli->cl_avail_grant) {
```

**Rationale:**
This is a straightforward variable name correction. The patch systematically renamed `target_bytes` to `tgt_bytes` throughout the function (visible in the function signature and other usages on lines 839, 840, 856, 861, 862), but this one instance was inadvertently left with the old name. The fix ensures consistency with the rest of the refactored code and resolves the "undeclared identifier" compilation error.
